Question: In the planning of a new district in a township, it was decided to build a special community in the southeast, northwest, centered on the citizen park. These four communities are designated as cultural area, leisure area, commercial area and administrative service area. It is known that the administrative service area is southwest of the cultural area, and the cultural area is southeast of the leisure area. Based on the above statement, which of the following can be derived? (A) Civic Park is north of the administrative service area. (B) The leisure area is southwest of the cultural area. (C) The cultural district is in the northeast of the business district. (D) The business district is southeast of the leisure area.
Full Response: Reformatted_Question: In the planning of a new district in a township, it was decided to build a special community in the southeast, northwest, centered on the citizen park. These four communities are designated as cultural area, leisure area, commercial area and administrative service area. It is known that the administrative service area is southwest of the cultural area, and the cultural area is southeast of the leisure area. Based on the above statement, which of the following can be derived?\n(A) Civic Park is north of the administrative service area. (B) The leisure area is southwest of the cultural area. (C) The cultural district is in the northeast of the business district. (D) The business district is southeast of the leisure area.

Answer_Reasoning: We know from the information given that the following relationships exist among the areas:
- The administrative service area is southwest of the cultural area, which implies that if we move southeast from the administrative area, we will reach the cultural area.
- The cultural area is southeast of the leisure area, which means going northwest from the cultural area would take us to the leisure area.

Based on the directions provided, if the cultural area is southeast of the leisure area, it means that the leisure area must be northwest of the cultural area. This confirms that choice B is incorrect, as B states the opposite direction.

Considering option A, none of the information about the positions relative to the Civic Park is given, thus we cannot determine its position.

Option C states that the cultural area is northeast of the business district without any concrete information on the business district's position in relation to the cultural area, so this cannot be derived directly.

However, from the relationships: leisure area (northwest), cultural area (center), and administrative area (southwest), you can derive option D, since any area directly northwest of the cultural area and in turn southeast of the leisure area, would be where the business district must logically be located, establishing a sequence of positions centered on the cultural area.

Therefore, statement D is consistent with the information provided.

Final_Answer: {D}

Full Response: Reformatted_Question: There are five teams participating in the game. The audience had the following comments on the results: (1) The champion is either the Shannan team or the Jiangbei team. (2) The champion is neither Shanbei nor Jiangnan. (3) The champion is Jiangnan Team. (4) The champion is not the Shannan team. The result of the match showed that only one argument was correct, so who won the championship?\n(A) Shannan. (B) Jiangnan. (C) Shanbei. (D) Jiangbei.

Answer_Reasoning: Based on the information provided in the comments and the fact that only one statement is correct, we can analyze as follows:

1. If the champion is either Shannan or Jiangbei, then statements (2), (3), and (4) must be false. However, if this statement were the true one, statement (4), which claims that the champion is not the Shannan team, would also be true if Shannan were the champion. Therefore, statement (1) cannot be the true statement as it would not lead to only one true statement overall.

2. If the champion is neither Shanbei nor Jiangnan, then statements (1), (3), and (4) must be false. If this statement were true, it would suggest that either Shannan or Jiangbei won. However, for only one statement to be true, Shannan cannot be the champion because that would make statement (4) true as well. This means statement (2) can be true if Jiangbei is the champion.

3. If the champion is Jiangnan, then statements (1), (2), and (4) would be false. However, that would leave more than one statement possibly true (e.g., if statement (3) is true, statement (2) is false regarding Jiangnan, but statement (1) could have a partially true aspect related to Jiangbei). Therefore, statement (3) cannot be correct without causing overlap with other statements.

4. If the champion is not the Shannan team, and this were the only true statement, then statements (1), (2), and (3) would need to be false. If Shannan is not the winner, and the only statement that can allow only one true statement without conflict is the second possibility under statement (2) with a result of Jiangbei being the champion.

Thus, the only scenario that fits with having exactly one correct statement is option D, indicating that Jiangbei won the championship.

Question: A research report shows that the proportion of children of cadres in Peking University increased from 20% in the 1980s to nearly 40% in 1977, surpassing the children of workers, farmers and professional technicians, and becoming the largest source of students. According to this, some media believe that the proportion of students and children of Peking University students has been rising for 20 years, surpassing other classes. Which one, if true, most doubts the views of the above media. (A) Many of the cadres counted in the past 20 years are enterprise cadres, which used to include only government officials. (B) Compared with foreign countries, Chinese education provides workers and peasants with more opportunities for education and social mobility. (C) After the founding of New China, more and more children of workers and peasants entered the university. (D) Some of the workers ’children in the statistics may be former farmers’ children.
Full Response: Reformatted_Question: A research report shows that the proportion of children of cadres in Peking University increased from 20% in the 1980s to nearly 40% in 1977, surpassing the children of workers, farmers, and professional technicians, and becoming the largest source of students. According to this, some media believe that the proportion of students and children of Peking University students has been rising for 20 years, surpassing other classes. Which one, if true, most doubts the views of the above media?\n
(A) Many of the cadres counted in the past 20 years are enterprise cadres, which used to include only government officials.
(B) Compared with foreign countries, Chinese education provides workers and peasants with more opportunities for education and social mobility.
(C) After the founding of New China, more and more children of workers and peasants entered the university.
(D) Some of the workers’ children in the statistics may be former farmers’ children.

Answer_Reasoning: The media perspective relies on the assertion that the proportion of children of cadres has been consistently rising and surpassing other groups. To doubt this view, one must find a statement that can provide an alternative explanation for the perceived trend.

Option A introduces the possibility that the definition of "cadres" has changed over the years to include a broader category, namely "enterprise cadres," not just "government officials." This implies that what might seem like an increase in the proportion of children of cadres could be attributed to the expanded definition, rather than a genuine trend of growing dominance over time.

Option B compares China with other countries, offering broader global context, but it doesn't directly challenge the internal dynamics of cadre representation in higher education within China.

Option C focuses on the general trend post-establishment of New China, highlighting increased access for other demographics (workers and peasants) without refuting the statistics concerning cadre children specifically.

Option D raises a point about misclassification in statistics, but it pertains to children of farmers being included among workers' children, which doesn't directly address the comparison or rise of cadre children.

Therefore, option A most effectively introduces doubt by suggesting that the observation of increasing cadre representation in Peking University could be a statistical artifact rather than an actual shift, by changing what "cadres" means.

Question: By analyzing the light released or absorbed by the atoms of an object, you can measure whether the object is far away from the earth or close to the earth. When the object is far away from the earth, the frequency of these lights will move to the red end (low frequency) of the spectrum, referred to as "red shift" "On the contrary, it is called" blue shift ". The unique light emitted by the atoms is also affected by the mass of the elementary particles that make up the atoms, especially the electrons. If the mass of an atom increases, the energy of the photons it releases will also become higher, so the release and absorption frequencies will be blue-shifted. Conversely, if the particles become lighter and lighter, the frequency will be red-shifted. Astronomical observations have found that most galaxies have a redshift phenomenon. Moreover, the farther the galaxy is from the earth, the greater the redshift. According to this, many scientists believe that the universe must be constantly expanding. It was human activities that led to their extinction.

Full Response: Reformatted_Question: Mr. Chen is going to hold a gathering of friends and family. Answer_Reasoning: Let's analyze the relationships Mr. Chen has invited:

1. Mr. Chen's father's brother-in-law could either be Mr. Chen's uncle or his father’s sister’s husband.
2. Mr. Chen's brother-in-law's father would be Mr. Chen's father-in-law if Mr. Chen's sister is married to his brother-in-law.
3. Mr. Chen's brother's mother-in-law could be Mr. Chen's own mother if Mr. Chen's brother is married to his wife.
4. His brother-in-law's brother could be either Mr. Chen’s brother-in-law again if it's referring to the same family or another separate person if the brother-in-law has a brother.

Upon examining these potential overlaps and relationships, it seems that the people Mr. Chen invited potentially overlap, therefore:

- His father's brother-in-law could already be accounted as his brother-in-law's father.
- His brother-in-law’s brother could technically be his brother-in-law, making no additional guest.

However, using specific information without overlap considering this reasoning:

- His father's brother-in-law: 1 guest
- His brother-in-law's father: 1 guest
- His brother's mother-in-law: 1 guest
- His brother-in-law's brother: if not overlapping, another guest

So potentially, he invited 4 different perspectives, but considering familial overlap effectively selects 3 unique guests.

The following assumptions can make the above inference hold, except. (A) Wang Wu's bonus is higher than Li Si's. (B) Li Si's bonus is higher than Miao Xiaoqin's. (C) Li Si's bonus is higher than Wang Wu's. (D) Li Si's bonus is as high as Wang Wu's.
Full Response: Reformatted_Question: Zhang Shan received a higher bonus than Li Si. Wang Wu's bonus was higher than Miao Xiaoqin's. Zhang Shan's bonus was also higher than Miao Xiaoqin. The following assumptions can make the above inference hold, except.\n(A) Wang Wu's bonus is higher than Li Si's. (B) Li Si's bonus is higher than Miao Xiaoqin's. (C) Li Si's bonus is higher than Wang Wu's. (D) Li Si's bonus is as high as Wang Wu's.

Answer_Reasoning: From the premises, we know that:

- Zhang Shan's bonus > Li Si's bonus.
- Wang Wu’s bonus > Miao Xiaoqin’s bonus.
- Zhang Shan’s bonus > Miao Xiaoqin’s bonus.

To find out which assumption cannot make the statement hold, let's examine each option:

- (A) Wang Wu's bonus is higher than Li Si's: This does not affect Zhang Shan's bonus directly, but it is possible if Zhang Shan has a higher bonus than Li Si, and Wang Wu also has a higher bonus than Miao Xiaoqin.
- (B) Li Si's bonus is higher than Miao Xiaoqin's: This fits the conclusion as it maintains the hierarchy Zhang Shan > Li Si > Miao Xiaoqin.
- (C) Li Si's bonus is higher than Wang Wu's: In this case, the conclusion may not hold because Zhang Shan might still have a higher bonus than Miao Xiaoqin through Li Si.
- (D) Li Si's bonus is as high as Wang Wu's: If Li Si has a bonus as high as Wang Wu's, it's possible for Zhang Shan to have a higher bonus than both, which doesn't contradict the main conclusion.

The exception is therefore option (C), as Li Si being greater than Wang Wu could create a conflict in the hierarchy of bonuses and might disrupt the ordering needed to ensure Zhang Shan's bonus is higher than Miao Xiaoqin's. Thus, option (C) is the assumption that does not necessarily support the conclusion.

Since the conclusion of "friends like dung" is not true, it can be logically derived?\n(A) The expression "money is like dung" is false. (D) Beijing University of Aeronautics and Astronautics.

- If Professor Qian is completely wrong, then the champion would be the Tsinghua University team or not the University of Science and Technology of China.

Question: Koreans love sauerkraut and Cuihua loves sauerkraut, so Cuihua is Korean. Which of the following options most clearly shows the absurdity of the above reasoning? (A) All Cretans are lying, John is Cretan, so John is lying. (B) Walking animals have legs, and tables have legs, so tables are walking animals. (C) Nishimura loves Cuihua. Cuihua loves pickled cabbage. Therefore, Nishimura loves pickled cabbage. (D) All gold glitters, so some glitters are gold.
Full Response: Reformatted_Question: Koreans love sauerkraut and Cuihua loves sauerkraut, so Cuihua is Korean. Which of the following options most clearly shows the absurdity of the above reasoning?\n(A) All Cretans are lying, John is Cretan, so John is lying. (B) Walking animals have legs, and tables have legs, so tables are walking animals. (C) Nishimura loves Cuihua. Cuihua loves pickled cabbage. Therefore, Nishimura loves pickled cabbage. (D) All gold glitters, so some glitters are gold.

Answer_Reasoning: The original statement assumes that because Cuihua loves something (sauerkraut) that is commonly liked by Koreans, Cuihua must also be Korean. This is a classic example of faulty logic known as affirming the consequent, where a specific condition being true leads to an erroneous generalization. Option (B) makes a similar logical error: just because tables share a characteristic with walking animals (having legs), it does not imply that tables are walking animals. This mirrors the mistake in the original reasoning, where a shared characteristic leads to an incorrect categorical inclusion.

Question: There are six switches S, T, W, X, Y, and Z in a circuit. The following conditions must be met when using these switches? If S and Z are now connected at the same time, which of the following must be true? (A) T is the on state and Y is the off state. (B) Both T and Y are off. (C) Both W and T are on. (D) X is the on state and Y is the off state.
Full Response: Reformatted_Question: There are six switches S, T, W, X, Y, and Z in a circuit. The following conditions must be met when using these switches: (1) If W is on, then X must be on; (2) Only off Turn on S to turn off T; (3) T and X cannot be connected at the same time, nor can they be turned off at the same time; (4) If Y and Z are turned on at the same time, then W must also be turned on. If S and Z are now connected at the same time, which of the following must be true? \n(A) T is the on state and Y is the off state. (B) Both T and Y are off. (C) Both W and T are on. (D) X is the on state and Y is the off state.

Answer_Reasoning: Given that S and Z are connected at the same time and the following considerations:

- If S is turned on, it may not necessarily impact T directly unless it's used to turn off T, but we also need to consider that it might be part of how the circuit operates.
- If Y and Z are on together, then W must also be on.

Given the third condition where T and X cannot be on or off at the same time, and knowing Z is on, the possible combination prevents T from being on. Therefore, T is off.

Now, consider options:

- (A) T is the on state and Y is the off state: T cannot be on because it contradicts the conditions with Z being on.
- (B) Both T and Y are off: With S and Z being on, T must be off due to the inability to turn it on simultaneously with Z being on and complying with other conditions.
- (C) Both W and T are on: T cannot be on when Z is on due to the Z→W dependency in the circuit logic.
- (D) X is the on state and Y is the off state: Given conditions (1) W on requires X to be on, and the dependency W→Y in part bypasses Y being needed to on.

Considering these factors, particularly the implications of the switches and compliance with conditions, the correct answer is that when S and Z are connected, T and Y both must be off.

If only one of the above three sentences is true, which of the following must be true? (A) Neither Mr Zhang nor Ms Wang bought Mongolian knives. (B) Mr. Zhang bought a Mongolian knife, but Ms. Wang did not. (C) Mr. Li of the tour group bought a Mongolian knife. (D) Both Mr Zhang and Ms Wang bought Mongolian knives.
Full Response: Reformatted_Question: A tourist group travels to Mulan paddock. The members ride horses, archery, eat barbecue and finally go to the shop to buy souvenirs. Known: (1) Someone bought a Mongolian knife. (2) Someone did not buy a Mongolian knife. (3) Both Mr. Zhang and Ms. Wang of the regiment bought Mongolian knives. If only one of the above three sentences is true, which of the following must be true?\n(A) Neither Mr Zhang nor Ms Wang bought Mongolian knives. (B) Mr. Zhang bought a Mongolian knife, but Ms. Wang did not. (C) Mr. Li of the tour group bought a Mongolian knife. (D) Both Mr Zhang and Ms Wang bought Mongolian knives.

Answer_Reasoning: We need to determine which one of the three given sentences is true.

1. Analysis of Statement 1 (): If only this statement is true, it means some member of the tourist group bought a Mongolian knife. However, if this were true, it would contradict the need for sentence (3) to be false, as it could still be someone other than Mr. Zhang and Ms. Wang who bought the knife. Given the logical contradictions introduced by considering each statement individually, we infer:
- If statement (1) is false, then it implies that not someone, but perhaps two people bought knives.
- If statement (2) is false, it matches the situation that "no one did not buy," implying at least two people bought knives.
- Since statement (3) must be false (because if true, it would corroborate statement (1)), then it must indeed be the case that no one or only one person could buy, contradicting statement (3) specifically about both by necessity not being true.

Thus, the consistent outcome is that statement (3) being false indicates neither Mr. Zhang nor Ms. Wang bought knives. Therefore, both statements (1) and (2) contribute to a plausible scenario where nobody or others besides Mr. Zhang and Ms. Wang bought the knives.

Based on the above questions, which of the following options for night duty is true?\n(A) Wu on Sunday. (B) The money is on Tuesday. (C) Lee is on Tuesday. (D) Sun is on Friday.

Answer_Reasoning: From the question facts:

1. We know Zheng is on Thursday (fact9).

2. Since Zheng is between Qian and Sun (fact8), Qian must be on Tuesday or Monday, and Sun must be on Friday or Saturday.

3. If Qian is on Monday, then Wang must be on Thursday, which is not possible because Zheng is on Thursday. Therefore, Qian is on Tuesday.

4. If Qian is on Tuesday, then Wang is on Friday (fact7).

5. If Sun is one day before Zhao (fact5), and since Wang is on Friday, Sun would be on Saturday, and Zhao would be on Sunday.

6. This leaves Li and Wu, where Li is two days later than Wu (fact6). Previously filled days exclude any other possibilities except Wu on Wednesday and Li on Saturday.

By examining the facts and filling the schedule correctly:

- Monday: Wu
- Tuesday: Qian
- Wednesday: Zhao
- Thursday: Zheng
- Friday: Wang
- Saturday: Sun
- Sunday: Li

(A) Wu on Sunday is incorrect.

(B) Qian on Tuesday is correct (fact11).

(C) Li on Tuesday is incorrect.

(D) Sun on Friday is incorrect.

(A) David will go to Cantor because he will get $ 150,000 more in two years. (B) David will go to Huizhong Company because he will get more than 50,000 US dollars every year. (C) David will go to Cantor because he will spend an extra $ 50,000 per year. (D) David will go to Huizhong Company because he will spend an extra $ 70,000 every year.

**Huizhong Company:**

- Initial half-year salary: $500,000
- First-year salary: $500,000 + ($500,000 + $50,000) = $1,050,000
- Second-year salary: ($500,000 + $100,000) + ($500,000 + $150,000) = $1,300,000
- Total for two years: $1,050,000 (first year) + $1,300,000 (second year) = $2,350,000

**Kang Tuo Company:**

- First-year salary: $1,000,000
- Second-year salary: $1,000,000 + $200,000 = $1,200,000
- Total for two years: $1,000,000 (first year) + $1,200,000 (second year) = $2,200,000

Comparing the two, David earns $150,000 more with Huizhong Company over two years ($2,350,000 - $2,200,000 = $150,000).

Considering David is looking for the best pay, he will choose Huizhong Company because it offers $150,000 more over two years, which disproves options that suggest he would choose Kang Tuo. Therefore, none of the provided options directly correspond to the correct rationale based on the figures, and the best logical conclusion is that David will choose Huizhong for the higher total salary.

Answer_Reasoning: To determine which set of players can participate, we must adhere to the conditions provided:

1. E or F has one person to participate, but not both: For each option, only one of E or F can be included, never both.

2. One of J or K will participate, but not both: Any set of players can only include J or K, not both.

3. If J participates, then G participates: If J is chosen, G must be included in the team.

4. Unless F participates, M does not participate: For M to be in the team, F must also be included.

- Option (A) E, F, H, K: Both E and F are selected, violating condition .

- Option (B) E, H, J, M: J is selected, so G must also be included (violating condition ), and M is selected without F being selected (violating condition ).

- Option (C) E, G, J, M: E is selected, not F, satisfying condition . J is selected, so G is selected, satisfying condition . However, M is selected without F being selected, which violates condition .

- Option (D) F, H, K, M: F is selected, not E, satisfying condition . K is selected, not J, satisfying condition . M is selected because F is also present, satisfying condition .

Therefore, the only option that meets all the conditions is Option (D) F, H, K, M.
